<p>Predict the Next Word</p>

<section data-state="sub-section" data-transition="linear" data-transition-speed="default">
<h2>Introduction</h2>
<div class="slideContent" >
<p><span style="color:blue; font-weight:bold; font-size:0.7em">This presentation is created as part of the requirement for the Coursera Data Science Capstone Course. </span></p>
<p><font size="5">
The goal of the project is to build a predictive text model combined with a shiny app UI that will predict the next word as the user types a sentence similar to the way most smart phone keyboards are implemented today using the technology of Swiftkey.</p>
<p><em>[Shiny App]</em> - [<a href="https://phng.shinyapps.io/capstone">https://phng.shinyapps.io/capstone</a>]</p>
<p><em>[Github Repo]</em> - [<a href="https://github.com/justusfrantz/capstone">https://github.com/justusfrantz/capstone</a>]</p>
<p></font></p>
</div>
</section>
<section data-state="sub-section" data-transition="linear" data-transition-speed="default">
<h2>Getting &amp; Cleaning the Data</h2>
<div class="slideContent" >
<p><span style="color:blue; font-weight:bold; font-size:0.7em">Before building the word prediction algorithm, data are first processed and cleaned as steps below:</span></p>
<p><font size="5"></p>
<ul>
<li>A subset of the original data was sampled from the three sources (blogs,twitter and news) which is then merged into one.</li>
<li>Next, data cleaning is done by conversion to lowercase, strip white space, and removing punctuation and numbers.</li>
<li>The corresponding n-grams are then created (Quadgram,Trigram and Bigram).</li>
<li>Next, the term-count tables are extracted from the N-Grams and sorted according to the frequency in descending order.</li>
<li>Lastly, the n-gram objects are saved as R-Compressed files (.RData files).</li>
</ul>
<p></font></p>
</div>
</section>
<section data-state="sub-section" data-transition="linear" data-transition-speed="default">
<h2>Word Prediction Model</h2>
<div class="slideContent" >
<p><span style="color:blue; font-weight:bold;font-size:0.7em">The prediction model for next word is based on the Katz Back-off algorithm. Explanation of the next word prediction flow is as below:</span></p>
<p><font size="5"></p>
<ul>
<li>Compressed data sets containing descending frequency sorted n-grams are first loaded.</li>
<li>User input words are cleaned in the similar way as before prior to prediction of the next word.</li>
<li>For prediction of the next word, Quadgram is first used (first three words of Quadgram are the last three words of the user provided sentence).</li>
<li>If no Quadgram is found, back off to Trigram (first two words of Trigram are the last two words of the sentence).</li>
<li>If no Trigram is found, back off to Bigram (first word of Bigram is the last word of the sentence)</li>
<li>If no Bigram is found, back off to the most common word with highest frequency &#39;the&#39; is returned.</li>
</ul>
<p></font></p>
</div>
</section>
<section data-state="sub-section" data-transition="linear" data-transition-speed="default">
<h2>Shiny Application</h2>

};

}

});

// notify container
if (window.notifySlideChanged)
notifySlideChanged(event.indexh)
} );
Reveal.addEventListener( 'slidechanged', function( event ) {
// notify container
if (window.notifySlideChanged)
notifySlideChanged(event.indexh)

if (window.MathJax)
window.MathJax.Hub.Rerender(event.currentSlide);
});
// forward command key events to the rstudio frame
window.onkeydown = function(e) {
// allow 'o' to toggle overview mode
switch( e.keyCode ) {
case 79: case 42: window.Reveal.toggleOverview(); break;
}
if (window.parent.presentationKeydown)
window.parent.presentationKeydown(e);
}

// bail if autosize is disabled
if (!false)

window.location.reload(true);
}, 300);
}
